B. Material Processed

In October, the Station was provided by the’ LIENVOY LP with 138
pages of daily resumes, from all lines, 15 pages of resumes from the Cuban
lines, 17 pages from the Czech lines and 121 pages from the Soviet lines,

In addition the taped reels from the Sovict and Czech lines were turned over
for the transcription of the Russtan and Czech conversations, There were
also provided 44 picces of other miscellaneous material,

- C, Liaison

Because of the urgency of business during the month of Octeber, thy
COS met with LIERGO and LIELEGANT more frequently, LITENSOR ex~
préssed his -grateluliess through LIELEGANT on providing him with reports®
on the political scene in the Far East counter les that be had visited, On 25

October, LITENSOR was given the report on the Cuban situation which was.
sent to the Station In DIR 44302, LITENSOR was also shown photos af the
ceting with high-level Mexican officials,
397 on thelr attitudes of the ULS..

ssile

Sovict missile bases in Cuba, Atter a

B, Material Processed

In August, the LIENVOY LP provided the Statton with 133 pages of
_ dally resumes, 40 pages of resumes from the Cuban lines and 35 other
pieces of matertal. There were also provided 115 pages of resumes from
the Soviet Hines and 63 pages from the Czech lines,

C. Exploitation of Material : :
The following-are exaniples of information obtaincd through LIENVOY.

1, Ina telephone conversation from San Luis Potosi, Col,
Renato Vega Amador, DFS Chief, told Capt. de la Barrera of the
Mexico City DFS: that "things are happening in San.Luis Potosi”,
and that “something’bad would happen” In Monterrey and Mexico
City against the Federal Government and that of the State of San
Luis Potost, (MEXI 1600)

2,. Joe Nordmann, Secretary of the International Assocation of
Democratic Lawyers (IADL}. spoke with Angetica Arenal de Alfaro
Siquciro# about his plan to see the President of Mexico to have David
Alfaro Siquetros released from prison. (MEXL 1676)

3. According to employees of the Prensa Latina, employees had
not been paid for some time and the financial situation of the Agency
was "desperate", (MEXI 1676)

D. Liaison i : ine E i‘

On 3 August, Chief of Station met with LITENSOR to give him a re-
port on Cuauhtemoc Cardenas, Through LIELEGANT on 8 August, Chief
of Siation was told that Cardenas would not be a candidate for “Water
Commissloner’ in the Mexicall area, (MEXT 1652)

In MEXI 1773, it was requested of Headquarters that briefing papers
vn Indonesia, Japan ‘and India be made available for LITENSOR's use on

hls approaching visit to these countries in late September, These were
pouched io Mexico City Chief of Station accordig to DIR 31814,

daily resumes, 61 tapes from three Czech lines, 100 tapes from four Soviet
Embassy lines with the transcriptions of the Spanish conversations, 66 trans~
cripttons from Cuban Embassy lines and 32 pteces of other material,

keep all equipment operating continuously and effictently,

indedd, doing a good fob of reviewing the LIFMVOY take, following up leads :
and forwarding positive information to-Headquartecs,

2, Regarding the operational exploitation of LIENVOY, it was obvious
that the Statica is avare of the operational leads presented through LISNVOY
but tt fe realized that the Mexico City Station probably does not have the
sents to prouptly follow up all the leads presented, while Headquacters
does not wish to place a burden on the Station by requesting detailed reporting
on tho action teken on LISWVOY leads, Headquarters fecle that the Station wight
inform Headquarters with. soae regularity what ts being done, It is suggested
that the Station include tn its Monthly Activities Report under Section A,
“Gxploitation of Material Obtained", general statecents concerning any out~
atanding exploitation of leads, sueh as is done {n the LIVAAT Monthly

* Reports (soa: HAMA-15595, 31 August 1960),

roporta received fron the Station during the period vf 1 October through
D1 Decauber 1960, over 50 indicated LIESVOY as their source which points up
the fact that LIENVOY produces approxtaately one-third cf the Station’a

10 August 1960

MEMORANDUM FOR: Chieg WHS

SUBJECT: |, CW Signals on Telephone Tap

REFERENCE: HMMA-14977, 13 May 1960

1, Atechnical analysis of referenceltap indicates that the
CW Morse signals probably were picked up incidental to the primary
tap and did not actually occur on Line #2, This is borne out both
from a technical standpoint (signal to noise ratio, extraneous CW
signals, ete.) as well as from the context of the messages them-
selves, The latter, ag will be noted in the attached transcript,
primarily concern arrivals ‘and departures of what appear to be
small maritime vessels, The two radio calls mentioned, i.e.
"XBRB2" and "XBRP", are listed in the International Call Sign
Book as follows:

XBRB - Vera Cruz ¥19-10N, 96-15)
XBRP = Pichilingue (24-12N, 110-20 Wy

The originating station in this case was Pichilingue,

2. Wad ake ore is some good reason why a port
authority on the west coast of Mexico would be sending traffic of
this nature to an caut coast port, However, just how these _
particular signals happened to be picked up ot'Sam Brooks! line
is open to conjecture, It is our guess that it probably was due
to one of the following reasons:

a, Aradio tranamitter may be situated near the
tap and is serving as a relay station between Pichilingue
and Vera Gruz, If this is the case it may be giving off
strong radio frequency signals which possibly are being
rectified by the tap itself,



an

225

b, The equipment used in conjunction with the tap

may be servitig as a poor radio receivar, using the telephone

line as au antenna,

€. The CW signals possibly are being picked up
inductively, i.e. from another phone line which is in
close proximity to Line §2, This theory seems-unlikely,
however, since the transmission of CW signals from one
coast to the other via telephone Lines would be a slow and
impractical procedure,

he afyaarWers
3, From ‘the standpoint of technical interost, wo" would

appreciate being advised if and when the & 5 able to iis
stantiate any of the above conjectures, ne tase

furnish additional analysis and ponte should ens figeaie
be noted in the future.

WILLIAM K, HARVEY
Chiei, FI/ Division D
